               <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>In view of this intriguing structure evolution for 1D CNF, the variations of electrochemical properties were carried out as presented in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs595-fig-0007">7</a>. The cycling stability of CNF-400/500/600/700 at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> was displayed in Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0007">7</a>A. Due to the excellent structural features (e.g., high degree of crystalline lattice and long-term disordered lattice), CNF-700 shows a reversible capacity of 240.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, larger than those of CNF-400/500/600 (128.3, 211.7, and 228.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0007">7</a>B displays the initial discharge–charge platform curves of CNF-700, and it possesses the discharge–charge capacities of 535 and 274.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a coulombic efficiency (CE) of 51.4%. Although the first sodiation–desodiation capacities were found for other electrodes, the lower CE values were obtained as 30.3%, 42.1%, and 40.9%, mainly derived from different special surface areas in Figure 12S (Supporting Information). Moreover, with the improved annealing temperatures, the voltage platforms were lowered in the order of CNF-400 (1.24 V) &gt; CNF-500 (1.01 V) &gt; CNF-600 (0.94 V) &gt; CNF-700 (0.75 V), which are beneficial for the enlarged energy density. Note that the largest CE and lowest voltage platforms of CNF-700 are crucial for the practical applications. Clearly, the outstanding rate performance (111.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>) can be noticed for CNF-700, which is ascribed to the introduction of effective defect, the expanded lattice space, and the increased lattice domain, facilitating the ion/electrons diffusion.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0043_R_d68468175e2990" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Power Sources Chin. Phys. B Energy Storage Mater. Nat. Commun.">43</a></span> In addition, it is noteworthy that their following cycling is still stable at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, demonstrating the best reversible properties. Even at a large current density of 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the satisfactory cyclic stability of CNF-700 (158.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) is exhibited after 2000 cycles, obviously higher than those of other electrodes.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs595-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/956d1587-5dbc-42d3-96ed-e1cd0e24befc/advs595-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/956d1587-5dbc-42d3-96ed-e1cd0e24befc/advs595-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0d4e19cf-eb81-477f-9cc1-8d87e6f18e16/advs595-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/956d1587-5dbc-42d3-96ed-e1cd0e24befc/advs595-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs595-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800080" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">A) The cycling performances, B) Coulombic efficiency, C,E) and rate properties of 0D CQDs, 1D CNF, 2D CNS, and 3D CFW, and D) the discharge platforms of 1D CNF.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">According to the aforementioned discussions, numerous differences on the characteristics were found for 1/2/3D samples from the evolution of 0D CQDs, further giving rise to the distinctions of the electrochemical kinetics. In Figure 13S (Supporting Information), the disappeared reduction peaks at first curves are due to the formation of SEI film with the decomposition of the electrolyte.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0044_R_d68468175e3018" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">44</a></span> After the first charge/discharge process, it is clear that the second, third, and fourth curves are overlapped, indicating that the stable SEI film is accomplished. Through the assistances of the cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves at different scan rates, two types of energy storage modes (SCP and DIP) were analyzed and the corresponding ratios were quantified. In <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs595-fig-0008">8</a>A–C, three couples of peaks for the as-derived samples were clearly observed between 0.01 and 0.5 V (vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), and they are sharper in the order of CNF-400 &lt; CNF-500 &lt; CNF-600 &lt; CNF-700, and 1D-CNF-700 &gt; 2D &gt; 3D, indicating the reduction of sodium storage in the graphite layers, which is ascribed to the variation of lattice interlayer in Table <a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#advs595-tbl-0001">1</a>.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0045_R_d68468175e3030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Sci. Rep.">45</a></span> These further demonstrate that the sodium ions insert/extract into graphite layers or microspores at low potential, which is consistence with the previous work.[<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0025_R_d68468175e3032" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Nano J. Mater. Chem. A">25</a>, <a href="#advs595-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0046_R_d68468175e3032" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Carbon">46</a></span>] At low potential, the oxidation peak of 1D CNF-700 is clearly sharper than that of 2/3D samples and that is gradually enhanced from CNF-400 to CNF-700 in Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0008">8</a>A–C. It is reasonable that the ordered graphitization lattice with the largest interlayer would provide numerous sodium-insertion channels, favoring the electrochemical performances.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0035_R_d68468175e3037" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a></span> It is interesting to note that all the peak shapes of the samples are nearly identical even through the voltages rising from 0.1 to 9.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, verifying small polarization at high rate current densities in Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0008">8</a> and Figure 14S (Supporting Information).<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0047_R_d68468175e3044" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Energy Mater.">47</a></span> Based on Dunn and co-workers' work,<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0048_R_d68468175e3046" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - J. Phys. Chem. C">48</a></span> the charge/discharge mechanism and the content of capacitive contribution can be quantified analyzed by Equations <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a> and <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a><div class="inline-equation" id="advs595-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/6938e9e7-e9c1-4023-92dd-5c5c98ae97a0/advs595-math-0001.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0001" title="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0001" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
               <div class="inline-equation" id="advs595-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/530cc199-613e-446d-888e-e81418ec05ff/advs595-math-0002.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0002" title="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0002" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs595-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f0cca802-c4e8-43f8-86a7-05f6c07bd998/advs595-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/f0cca802-c4e8-43f8-86a7-05f6c07bd998/advs595-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/aa858221-9380-4400-bf0f-d59ac31163ba/advs595-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f0cca802-c4e8-43f8-86a7-05f6c07bd998/advs595-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs595-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800080" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">CV curves at various scan rates, capacitive contribution of the total current (orange) for A1–A4) 1D CNF700/600/500/400, B) 2D CNS, C) 3D CFW, D) log <i>i</i> versus log <i>v</i> plots and separation of the capacitive and diffusion-controlled charges at 2 mV s<sup>–1</sup> in SIB (inset), and E) normalized contribution ratio of capacitive capacities at different scan rates for the as-prepared samples.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <p>Considering Equation <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>, the <i>b</i>-value close to 1 implies SCP, while that approaching 0.5 indicates DIP.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0035_R_d68468175e3084" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a></span> The fitting lines and <i>b</i>-values are shown in Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0008">8</a>D, revealing the stable electrochemical behaviors and enhanced capacitance-controlled ratios in sequence: CNF-400 &lt; CNF-500 &lt; CNF-600 &lt; CNF-700. Obviously, the largest <i>b</i>-value (0.84) is found for 1D CNF-700, illustrating that 1D CNF with most effective defects and largest lattice space was favored by SCP.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0049_R_d68468175e3093" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Nano Small Nat. Mater.">49</a></span> The effective defects could render more sodium-ion storage, and the large lattice distance could reduce the resistance of sodium ions' insertion/extraction, which is important for SCP behaviors. To further investigate the ratio of SCP and DIP for the total capacity at different scan rates, Equation <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a> is utilized, and <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> are associated with SCP and DIP, respectively. In the inset of Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0008">8</a>D and in Figure 15S (Supporting Information), the largest ratio of SCP for 1D CNF-700 samples is 87% at 0.9 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, which matches well with the results of the slope. In addition, the ratios of SCP increase at mounting scan rates, further conforming that the electrochemical properties are determined by SCP.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0050_R_d68468175e3111" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - ACS Nano">50</a></span> Thus, the strongest SCP was found for 1D CNF, which is corresponding to the best rate performances. Two reasons are deduced to explain the high SCP for 1D CNF: (1) much sodium ions' insertion entrances are provided by partial-ordered graphitize structures with large layer distance; (2) the existence of effective defects and micropores facilitates the reversible Na-adsorption/desorption on the surface.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0035_R_d68468175e3113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nano Energy">35</a></span></p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">To better understand the Na-storage behaviors at different cycles for the as-prepared samples, electrochemical impedance measurements (EIS) was conducted to confirm the corresponding sodium-ion coefficients (<i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub>). The resistances at undischarged condition are exhibited in Figure 16S (Supporting Information), where it is found that of 3D CFW is much larger than that of 1/2D samples and the resistance is decreasing for CNF-400/500/600/700. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs595-fig-0009">9</a>, two depressed semicircles appeared in the middle–high frequency regions, while a linear slope located at the low-frequency region in all impedance spectra, revealing the charge transfer resistance and Warburg diffusion of sodium ions in the internal of samples, respectively. Based on these commons features, the equivalent circuit (the inset of Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0009">9</a>D) was established to explore various components of impedance. This can be divided into four parts: (1) <i>R</i><sub>e</sub> is related to the resistance of the materials in cell; (2) <i>R</i><sub>f</sub> and <i>CPE1</i> are associated with the SEI films; (3) <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and <i>CPE2</i> are equivalent to the charge transfer resistance; and (4) <i>Z</i><sub>w</sub> as the important criterion for evaluating the speed of Na-transfer is presented by the linear slope. It is found that the total of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>f</sub> for 1D CNF is slight larger than that of 2D CNS, 3D CFW, which is ascribed that the high degree of graphitization would improve the electronic conductivity, giving rise to the small resistance. Moreover, the impedances of all the samples were decreased gradually with the increasing charge/discharge cycles, suggesting the decreasing resistances of electrode, which are beneficial for electron transferring. According to the Warburg factor related to <i>Z</i><sub>w</sub> (Equations <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0003" title="Link to equation">3</a> and <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0004" title="Link to equation">4</a>), the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><i><sub>+</sub></i> of all the curves was quantified and analyzed
               <div class="inline-equation" id="advs595-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/39979a3b-0acb-4e92-a039-60be5b517b95/advs595-math-0003.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0003" title="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0003" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
               <div class="inline-equation" id="advs595-disp-0004"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/9509c663-060f-4746-8f59-3e9b74894915/advs595-math-0004.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0004" title="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs595:advs595-math-0004" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs595-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c5710641-44ec-4832-a31e-b5f76a562bb6/advs595-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/c5710641-44ec-4832-a31e-b5f76a562bb6/advs595-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9b8db015-b13b-4ccf-9807-879b94822506/advs595-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c5710641-44ec-4832-a31e-b5f76a562bb6/advs595-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs595-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800080" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Nyquist plots at discharge stage (0.8 V) after different cycling, the fitting lines in the low frequency for A) 1D CNF, B) 2D CNS, C) 3D CFW. D) Impedance spectra and fitting curve using the equivalent circuit (inset). E) Sodium diffusion coefficients after various cycling for 1/2/3D samples.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <p>The fitting lines about <i>Z′</i> versus ω<sup>−1/2</sup> (<i>ω = 2πf</i>) were displayed in Figure 10S in the Supporting Information (A3, B3, C3), to further obtain σ. Obviously, the slopes of 1D CNF are smaller than those of other samples, and the larger the σ, the smaller the <i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub>. In addition, the <i>R</i> in Equation <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs595-disp-0004" title="Link to equation">4</a> is the gas constant (8.314 J mol<sup>−1</sup> K<sup>−1</sup>); <i>T</i>, <i>S</i>, <i>F</i>, <i>C</i> are the absolute temperature (297.15 K), the electrode surface area (1.15 cm<sup>2</sup>), the Faraday constant (96 485 A mol<sup>−1</sup>), and the concentration of electrolyte (1 mol L<sup>−1</sup>) respectively; and <i>n</i> is obtained from the equation (<i>Q</i> = <i>nF</i>/3.6<i>Mr</i>). Note that <i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub> of 1D CNF is much higher than that of 2/3D samples at various cycles in Figure <a href="#advs595-fig-0009">9</a>E. For examples, from Table 2S (Supporting Information), the <i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub> of 1D CNF at 100 cycles is 2.81 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, about nine times than that of 2D CNS (0.32 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) and three times than that of 3D CFW (0.91 × 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>), which facilitates the Na transfer in the internal of carbon samples.<span><a href="#advs595-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0037_R_d68468175e3257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Nano Energy">37</a>, <a href="#advs595-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs595-bib-0051_R_d68468175e3257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - J. Power Sources Electrochim. Acta.">51</a></span></p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="advs595-sec-0060">
         
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs595-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, controlling 1D CNF, 2D CNS, and 3D CFW is effectively addressed via the aid of temperature-induced intermediates of salts and the self-assembly of 0D CQDS. The catalytic characteristics of the reactant production (ZnO, Ni, and Cu) are vital for the in situ construction of multidimensional carbon samples through the “orient induction” of ZnO, the “dissolution–precipitation” of Ni, as well as the “surface adsorption self-limited” of Cu, further revealing that lattice spaces, the degree of graphitization, effective defects, and special surface area can be effectively manipulated. The formation mechanism of 1D CNF was further explored and deemed as the “vines' style” growth mechanism triggered by the high energy from the improved temperature. As expected, thanks to theses structure advantages, when 1/2/3D samples are used as anodes for SIBs, the electrochemical properties were greatly enhanced. 1D CNF shows the high reversible capacity of 324.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and it retains 301.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, as well as the excellent capacity (107 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 5000 cycles). Moreover, 2D CNS and 3D CFW display the good rate performance, delivering Na-storage capacities of 92.2 and 90.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 3000 cycles. The pseudocapacitive contributions are quantificationally analyzed to confirm the fundamental point of the fast Na<sup>+</sup> storage for 1D CNF. The construction of multidimensional carbon samples from the catalytic features shed light on the preparation of carbon structure and wide application.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="advs595-sec-0070">
         
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs595-sec-0070-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <p>All the chemicals in this work were obtained from the Aladdin and used without any purification.</p>
         
         <p><i>Preparation of 0D CQDs</i>: In this typical process, some modifications were carried out. With the magnetic stirring (400 rad min<sup>−1</sup>), 12 g of NaOH (Alpha) was reacted with 40 mL of acetone (Alpha) for 1 h. Then, the mixture was kept for 200 h in dry environment under ambient temperature and pressure. Through the acid leach with 1 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl solution, the neutral product was obtained, further centrifuged, and washed with deionized water for five times to get the final product. After drying for 24 h to remove the water, the CQDs' powder was achieved.</p>
         
         <p><i>Preparation of 1D CNF, 2D CNS, and 3D CFW</i>: The salts (ZnCl<sub>2</sub>, NiCl<sub>2</sub>, and CuCl) (Alpha) and CQDs were mixed thoroughly via grinding in an agate mortar with the ratio of 10:1 in weight. The as-prepared mixtures were calcined in a one-tube furnace under Ar atmosphere at 700 °C (400/500/600 °C) for 5 h, with a heating rate of 10 °C min<sup>−1</sup>. The mixture accompanied with ZnCl<sub>2</sub> was washed by magnetic stirring and ultrasonication with 1 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl solution for 12 h, further conducting suction filtration with water and ethanol washing to obtain 1D structures. The mixture with NiCl<sub>2</sub> was placed in the concentrated hydrochloric acid and stirred at 60 °C for 12 h, then washed with water and ethanol to neutralize and to get 2D sheets. The mixture containing CuCl was washed with FeCl<sub>3</sub> and 1 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl, further achieving the final product with water and ethanol. All the products were dried in a vacuum at 100 °C for over 12 h to prepare a 3D framework.</p>
         
         <p><i>Materials' Preparation</i>: A power X-ray diffractometer (Rigaku D/max 2550 VB+18 kW, Japan (Cu Kα radiation, λ = 0.1546 nm, <i>V</i> = 40 kV, <i>I</i> = 30 mA)), a Laser Micro-Raman spectrometer (Renishaw InVia, UK), an X-ray photoelectron spectrometer (K-Alpha 1063, UK) were used to characterize the crystalline structure of the as-obtained samples. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) (K-Alpha 1063) and FTIR (AVTA-TAR, 370) were used to analyze these functional groups. The surface morphologies and internal structure were investigated through SEM (a JEM-2100F instrument at 200 kV) and TEM.</p>
         
         <p><i>Electrochemical Tests</i>: In a MBraun glove box, the CR-2016 cells accompanied with Na metal (purity, 99.5%) as counter electrode were assembled to test the electrochemical properties of the as-obtained samples with argon concentrations of moisture and oxygen below 5 ppm. The active mass of every electrode was about 0.7–1.0 mg. The electrolytes were 1 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> in fluoroethylene carbonate: propylene carbonate) with the ratio of 95:5. Polypropylene (Celgard 2400) was used as a separator. Land CT 2001 battery and Arbin battery cycler (BT2000) were used to investigate the galvanostatic charge/discharged and rate performances at a series of current densities in the voltage window of 0.01–3.0 versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. EIS and CV) were carried out using the MULTI AUTOLAB M204 instruments under various conditions.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
